style="position: absolute; top: 0; right: 0; border: 0;"/>\n  </a>\n  <div class="container">\n   <div class="jumbotron text-center">\n    <h1>\n     ng-polymer-elements\n    </h1>\n    <p>\n     AngularJS two-way binding for Polymer Web Components\n    </p>\n    <p>\n     Out of the box support for Iron, Paper, Gold and Google elements\n    </p>\n    <div>\n     <a class="btn btn-default" <iframe data-gapiattached="true" frameborder="0" hspace="0" id="I0_1492352433769" marginheight="0" marginwidth="0" name="I0_1492352433769" ng-non-bindable="" scrolling="no" </div>\n     <iframe allowtransparency="true" class="twitter-share-button twitter-share-button-rendered twitter-tweet-button" data-url="https://gabiaxel.github.io/ng-polymer-elements" frameborder="0" id="twitter-widget-0" scrolling="no" style="position: static; visibility: visible; width: 61px; height: 20px;" title="Twitter Tweet Button">\n     </iframe>\n    </div>\n   </div>\n   <h3>\n    Why do I need it?\n   </h3>\n   <p>\n    AngularJS and Web Components both provide binding mechanisms, and for some cases you can bind the\n      scope properties to Web Components attributes. For example, the following code works fine:\n   </p>\n   <div class="row">\n    <div class="col-sm-6">\n     <pre class="prettyprint prettyprinted"><span class="pln">$scope</span><span class="pun">.</span><span class="pln">buttonLabel </span><span class="pun">=</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="str">\'Click me\'</span><span class="pun">;</span><span class="pln">\n\n$scope</span><span class="pun">.</span><span class="pln">buttonAction </span><span class="pun">=</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="kwd">function</span><span class="pun">()</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="pun">{</span><span class="pln">\n   alert</span><span class="pun">(</span><span class="str">\'Button clicked\'</span><span class="pun">);</span><span class="pln">\n</span><span class="pun">};</span></pre>\n     <pre class="prettyprint prettyprinted" ng-non-bindable=""><span class="tag">&lt;paper-button</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="atn">ng-click</span><span class="pun">=</span><span class="atv">"buttonAction()"</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="atn">raised</span><span class="tag">&gt;</span><span class="pln">\n  {{buttonLabel}}\n</span><span class="tag">&lt;/paper-button&gt;</span></pre>\n    </div>\n    <div class="col-sm-6 ng-scope" ng-controller="PlainExampleCtrl as ctrl">\n     <paper-button aria-disabled="false" class="x-scope paper-button-0" ng-click="ctrl.buttonAction()" raised="" role="button" tabindex="0">\n      <paper-ripple class="style-scope paper-button">\n       <div class="style-scope paper-ripple" id="background">\n       </div>\n       <div class="style-scope paper-ripple" id="waves">\n       </div>\n      </paper-ripple>\n      <paper-material animated="" class="content style-scope paper-button x-scope paper-material-0 ng-binding" elevation="1">\n       Click me\n      </paper-material>\n     </paper-button>\n    </div>\n   </div>\n   <p>\n    There are two cases where you can\'t get Web Components to work with your AngularJS models:\n   </p>\n   <ul>\n    <li>\n     Having Web Components update your model, for example\n     <pre class="prettyprint prettyprinted" ng-non-bindable=""><span class="tag">&lt;paper-input</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="atn">value</span><span class="pun">=</span><span class="atv">"{{myModel}}"</span><span class="tag">&gt;&lt;/paper-input&gt;</span><span class="pln"> </span></pre>\n     will not change\n     <code>\n      myModel\n     </code>\n     when the user changes the input text.\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     Binding anything other than a string, for example\n     <pre class="prettyprint prettyprinted" ng-non-bindable=""><span class="tag">&lt;google-map</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="atn">map</span><span class="pun">=</span><span class="atv">"{{myMap}}"</span><span class="tag">&gt;&lt;google-map&gt;</span></pre>\n     will not work because the expression\n     <code ng-non-bindable="">\n      {{myMap}}\n     </code>\n     will be treated as a string.\n    </li>\n   </ul>\n   Enters ng-polymer-elements.\n   <p>\n   </p>\n   <hr/>\n   <h3>\n    What does it do?\n   </h3>\n   <p>\n    ng-polymer-elements creates directives for existing custom elements, allowing you to use them as you would any directive.\n      The following example shows how you can use iron-input and paper-input with a model as if they were "plain" input:\n   </p>\n   <div class="row">\n    <div class="col-sm-6">\n     <pre class="prettyprint prettyprinted"><span class="tag">&lt;input</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="atn">type</span><span class="pun">=</span><span class="atv">"text"</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="atn">ng-model</span><span class="pun">=</span><span class="atv">"text"</span><span class="tag">/&gt;</span><span class="pln">\n</span><span class="tag">&lt;input</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="atn">is</span><span class="pun">=</span><span class="atv">"iron-input"</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="atn">ng-model</span><span class="pun">=</span><span class="atv">"text"</span><span class="tag">/&gt;</span><span class="pln">\n</span><span class="tag">&lt;paper-input</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="atn">ng-model</span><span class="pun">=</span><span class="atv">"text""&gt;</span><span class="tag">&lt;/paper-input&gt;</span></pre>\n    </div>\n    <div class="col-sm-6">\n     <div layout="" vertical="">\n      <input class="corm-control ng-pristine ng-untouched ng-valid" ng-model="text" placeholder="input" type="text"/>\n      <input class="ng-pristine ng-untouched ng-valid" is="iron-input" ng-model="text" placeholder="iron-input"/>\n      <paper-input aria-disabled="false" class="x-scope paper-input-0 ng-pristine ng-untouched ng-valid ng-isolate-scope" label="paper-input" ng-model="text">\n       <paper-input-container class="style-scope paper-input x-scope paper-input-container-0">\n        <span>\n        </span>\n        <div class="floated-label-placeholder style-scope paper-input-container">\n        </div>\n        <span>\n        </span>\n        <template class="style-scope paper-input-container" is="dom-if">\n        </template>\n        <div class="input-content style-scope paper-input-container">\n         <label class="style-scope paper-input" id="paper-input-label-253">\n          paper-input\n         </label>\n         <input aria-describedby="" aria-labelledby="paper-input-label-253" autocomplete="off" class="style-scope paper-input" id="input" is="iron-input" placeholder=""/>\n         <template class="style-scope paper-input" is="dom-if">\n         </template>\n         <template class="style-scope paper-input" is="dom-if">\n         </template>\n        </div>\n        <div class="underline style-scope paper-input-container">\n         <div class="unfocused-line fit style-scope paper-input-container">\n         </div>\n         <div class="focused-line fit style-scope paper-input-container">\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="add-on-content style-scope paper-input-container">\n        </div>\n       </paper-input-container>\n      </paper-input>\n     </div>\n    </div>\n   </div>\n   <hr/>\n   <h3>\n    How do I install it?\n   </h3>\n   <p>\n    Either install it with bower using\n    <code>\n     bower install ng-polymer-elements\n    </code>\n    or\n    <a href="https://github.com/GabiAxel/ng-polymer-elements/archive/0.3.0.zip">\n     download the release\n    </a>\n    .\n    <br/>\n    <br/>\n    Add\n    <code>\n     ng-polymer-elements\n    </code>\n    to your module\'s dependencies.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    ng-polymer-elements uses\n    <code>\n     Object.observe()\n    </code>\n    with properties of type\n    <code>\n     Object\n    </code>\n    and\n    <code>\n     Array\n    </code>\n    .\n      To support this on browsers that don\'t support\n    <code>\n     Object.observe()\n    </code>\n    , add a\n    <a href="https://github.com/MaxArt2501/object-observe">\n     polyfill\n    </a>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    The generated directives may be applied only after the custom elements have been registered.\n      This means that in browsers that don\'t support custom elements and rely on the polyfill, the generated directives\n      can be used only after the\n    <code>\n     WebComponentsReady\n    </code>\n    event has been fired. If the initial view of the Angular\n      application contains these directives, you may want to consider manual bootstrap like so:\n   </p>\n   <pre class="prettyprint prettyprinted"><span class="pln">window</span><span class="pun">.</span><span class="pln">addEventListener</span><span class="pun">(</span><span class="str">\'WebComponentsReady \'</span><span class="pun">,</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="kwd">function</span><span class="pun">()</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="pun">{</span><span class="pln">\n  angular</span><span class="pun">.</span><span class="pln">bootstrap</span><span class="pun">(</span><span class="pln">wrap</span><span class="pun">(</span><span class="pln">document</span><span class="pun">),</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="pun">[</span><span class="str">\'ng-polymer-elements-example\'</span><span class="pun">]);</span><span class="pln">\n</span><span class="pun">});</span></pre>\n   <hr/>\n   <h3>\n    Show me the magic!\n   </h3>\n   <p>\n    Out of the box ng-polymer-elements supports the following Polymer elements:\n   </p>\n   <table class="table">\n    <thead>\n     <tr>\n      <th>\n       Custom <td rowspan="3">\n       paper-input\n       <br/>\n       paper-textarea\n       <br/>\n       gold-email-input\n       <br/>\n       gold-phone-input\n       <br/>\n       gold-cc-expiration-input\n     </td>\n      <td>\n       ng-tab\n      </td>\n     </tr>\n    </tbody>\n   </table>\n   <hr/>\n   <p>\n    The following example shows the binding of a paper-radio-group selected value:\n   </p>\n   <div class="row">\n    <div class="col-sm-6">\n     <pre class="prettyprint prettyprinted" ng-non-bindable=""><span class="tag">&lt;paper-radio-group</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="atn">ng-model</span><span class="pun">=</span><span class="atv">"radio"</span><span class="tag">&gt;</span><span class="pln">\n   </span><span class="tag">&lt;paper-radio-button</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="atn">name</span><span class="pun">=</span><span class="atv">"one"</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="atn">label</span><span class="pun">=</span><span "ericbidelman"\n    }\n  ]\n}</pre>\n    </div>\n   </div>\n   <hr/>\n   <h3>\n    How do I use it with other custom elements?\n   </h3>\n   <p>\n    ng-polymer-elements uses a simple structure to map directive attributes to custom element properties.\n      You can extend the mapping by setting the\n    <code>\n     $ngPolymerMappings\n    </code>\n    constant in the\n    <code>\n     ng-polymer-elements\n    </code>\n    module with your mappings.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    The mapping structure is an object where the keys are the directive names, and their values are objects that contain a key\n      for each directive attribute you want to map. The values for the directives represent the custom element property or event,\n      and can be constant or defined in runtime for each instance of the directive.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    For constant mapping, use a string prefixed with "=" for property or "&amp;" for event, and the property/event name.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    For dynamic mapping, use a function named "property" or "event". The function received the element as a single argument\n      during the directive linking and returns a property/event name as string (without "="/"&amp;" prefix).\n   </p>\n   <pre class="prettyprint prettyprinted"><span class="pln">angular</span><span class="pun">.</span><span class="kwd">module</span><span class="pun">(</span><span class="str">\'ng-polymer-elements\'</span><span class="pun">).</span><span class="pln">constant</span><span class="pun">(</span><span class="str">\'$ngPolymerMappings\'</span><span class="pun">,</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="pun">{</span><span class="pln">\n  myElement</span><span class="pun">:</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="pun">{</span><span class="pln">\n    ngModel</span><span class="pun">:</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="kwd">function</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="kwd">property</span><span class="pun">(</span><span class="pln">element</span><span class="pun">)</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="pun">{</span><span class="pln">\n      </span><span class="kwd">return</span><span class="pln"> element</span><span class="pun">.</span><span class="pln">hasAttribute</span><span class="pun">(</span><span class="str">\'multi\'</span><span class="pun">)</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="pun">?</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="str">\'selectedValues\'</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="pun">:</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="str">\'selected\'</span><span class="pun">;</span><span class="pln">\n    </span><span class="pun">},</span><span class="pln">\n    ngChange</span><span class="pun">:</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="str">\'&amp;iron-change\'</span><span class="pln">\n  </span><span class="pun">}</span><span class="pln">\n</span><span class="pun">});</span></pre>\n   <p>\n    In this example we add support for\n    <code>\n     my-element\n    </code>\n    and map the\n    <code>\n     ng-model\n    </code>\n    attribute in runtime to either\n    <code>\n     selectedValue\n    </code>\n    or\n    <code>\n     selected\n    </code>\n    property, depending on the existence of the\n    <code>\n     multi\n    </code>\n    attribute,\n      and we map the\n    <code>\n     ng-change\n    </code>\n    attribute to the\n    <code>\n     iron-change\n    </code>\n    event.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    When mapping events, the original event will be available to AngularJS handlers as the\n    <code>\n     $event\n    </code>\n    parameter.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    See\n    <code>\n     allMappings\n    </code>\n    in\n    <a href="https://github.com/GabiAxel/ng-polymer-elements/blob/master/ng-polymer-elements.js">\n     ng-polymer-elements.js\n    </a>\n    for default mappings.\n   </p>\n  </div>\n  <script style="position: absolute; top: 0; right: 0; border: 0;"/>\n  </a>\n  <div class="container">\n   <div class="jumbotron text-center">\n    <h1>\n     ng-polymer-elements\n    </h1>\n    <p>\n     AngularJS two-way binding for Polymer Web Components\n    </p>\n    <p>\n     Out of the box support for Iron, Paper, Gold and Google elements\n    </p>\n    <div>\n     <a class="btn btn-default" <iframe data-gapiattached="true" frameborder="0" hspace="0" id="I0_1492574410489" marginheight="0" marginwidth="0" name="I0_1492574410489" ng-non-bindable="" scrolling="no" </div>\n     <iframe allowtransparency="true" class="twitter-share-button twitter-share-button-rendered twitter-tweet-button" data-url="https://gabiaxel.github.io/ng-polymer-elements" frameborder="0" id="twitter-widget-0" scrolling="no" style="position: static; visibility: visible; width: 61px; height: 20px;" title="Twitter Tweet Button">\n     </iframe>\n    </div>\n   </div>\n   <h3>\n    Why do I need it?\n   </h3>\n   <p>\n    AngularJS and Web Components both provide binding mechanisms, and for some cases you can bind the\n      scope properties to Web Components attributes. For example, the following code works fine:\n   </p>\n   <div class="row">\n    <div class="col-sm-6">\n     <pre class="prettyprint prettyprinted"><span class="pln">$scope</span><span class="pun">.</span><span class="pln">buttonLabel </span><span class="pun">=</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="str">\'Click me\'</span><span class="pun">;</span><span class="pln">\n\n$scope</span><span class="pun">.</span><span class="pln">buttonAction </span><span class="pun">=</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="kwd">function</span><span class="pun">()</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="pun">{</span><span class="pln">\n   alert</span><span class="pun">(</span><span class="str">\'Button clicked\'</span><span class="pun">);</span><span class="pln">\n</span><span class="pun">};</span></pre>\n     <pre class="prettyprint prettyprinted" ng-non-bindable=""><span class="tag">&lt;paper-button</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="atn">ng-click</span><span class="pun">=</span><span class="atv">"buttonAction()"</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="atn">raised</span><span class="tag">&gt;</span><span class="pln">\n  {{buttonLabel}}\n</span><span class="tag">&lt;/paper-button&gt;</span></pre>\n    </div>\n    <div class="col-sm-6 ng-scope" ng-controller="PlainExampleCtrl as ctrl">\n     <paper-button aria-disabled="false" class="x-scope paper-button-0" ng-click="ctrl.buttonAction()" raised="" role="button" tabindex="0">\n      <paper-ripple class="style-scope paper-button">\n       <div class="style-scope paper-ripple" id="background">\n       </div>\n       <div class="style-scope paper-ripple" id="waves">\n       </div>\n      </paper-ripple>\n      <paper-material animated="" class="content style-scope paper-button x-scope paper-material-0 ng-binding" elevation="1">\n       Click me\n      </paper-material>\n     </paper-button>\n    </div>\n   </div>\n   <p>\n    There are two cases where you can\'t get Web Components to work with your AngularJS models:\n   </p>\n   <ul>\n    <li>\n     Having Web Components update your model, for example\n     <pre class="prettyprint prettyprinted" ng-non-bindable=""><span class="tag">&lt;paper-input</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="atn">value</span><span class="pun">=</span><span class="atv">"{{myModel}}"</span><span class="tag">&gt;&lt;/paper-input&gt;</span><span class="pln"> </span></pre>\n     will not change\n     <code>\n      myModel\n     </code>\n     when the user changes the input text.\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     Binding anything other than a string, for example\n     <pre class="prettyprint prettyprinted" ng-non-bindable=""><span class="tag">&lt;google-map</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="atn">map</span><span class="pun">=</span><span class="atv">"{{myMap}}"</span><span class="tag">&gt;&lt;google-map&gt;</span></pre>\n     will not work because the expression\n     <code ng-non-bindable="">\n      {{myMap}}\n     </code>\n     will be treated as a string.\n    </li>\n   </ul>\n   Enters ng-polymer-elements.\n   <p>\n   </p>\n   <hr/>\n   <h3>\n    What does it do?\n   </h3>\n   <p>\n    ng-polymer-elements creates directives for existing custom elements, allowing you to use them as you would any directive.\n      The following example shows how you can use iron-input and paper-input with a model as if they were "plain" input:\n   </p>\n   <div class="row">\n    <div class="col-sm-6">\n     <pre class="prettyprint prettyprinted"><span class="tag">&lt;input</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="atn">type</span><span class="pun">=</span><span class="atv">"text"</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="atn">ng-model</span><span class="pun">=</span><span class="atv">"text"</span><span class="tag">/&gt;</span><span class="pln">\n</span><span class="tag">&lt;input</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="atn">is</span><span class="pun">=</span><span class="atv">"iron-input"</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="atn">ng-model</span><span class="pun">=</span><span class="atv">"text"</span><span class="tag">/&gt;</span><span class="pln">\n</span><span class="tag">&lt;paper-input</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="atn">ng-model</span><span class="pun">=</span><span class="atv">"text""&gt;</span><span class="tag">&lt;/paper-input&gt;</span></pre>\n    </div>\n    <div class="col-sm-6">\n     <div layout="" vertical="">\n      <input class="corm-control ng-pristine ng-untouched ng-valid" ng-model="text" placeholder="input" type="text"/>\n      <input class="ng-pristine ng-untouched ng-valid" is="iron-input" ng-model="text" placeholder="iron-input"/>\n      <paper-input aria-disabled="false" class="x-scope paper-input-0 ng-pristine ng-untouched ng-valid ng-isolate-scope" label="paper-input" ng-model="text">\n       <paper-input-container class="style-scope paper-input x-scope paper-input-container-0">\n        <span>\n        </span>\n        <div class="floated-label-placeholder style-scope paper-input-container">\n        </div>\n        <span>\n        </span>\n        <template class="style-scope paper-input-container" is="dom-if">\n        </template>\n        <div class="input-content style-scope paper-input-container">\n         <label class="style-scope paper-input" id="paper-input-label-969">\n          paper-input\n         </label>\n         <input aria-describedby="" aria-labelledby="paper-input-label-969" autocomplete="off" class="style-scope paper-input" id="input" is="iron-input" placeholder=""/>\n         <template class="style-scope paper-input" is="dom-if">\n         </template>\n         <template class="style-scope paper-input" is="dom-if">\n         </template>\n        </div>\n        <div class="underline style-scope paper-input-container">\n         <div class="unfocused-line fit style-scope paper-input-container">\n         </div>\n         <div class="focused-line fit style-scope paper-input-container">\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="add-on-content style-scope paper-input-container">\n        </div>\n       </paper-input-container>\n      </paper-input>\n     </div>\n    </div>\n   </div>\n   <hr/>\n   <h3>\n    How do I install it?\n   </h3>\n   <p>\n    Either install it with bower using\n    <code>\n     bower install ng-polymer-elements\n    </code>\n    or\n    <a href="https://github.com/GabiAxel/ng-polymer-elements/archive/0.3.0.zip">\n     download the release\n    </a>\n    .\n    <br/>\n    <br/>\n    Add\n    <code>\n     ng-polymer-elements\n    </code>\n    to your module\'s dependencies.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    ng-polymer-elements uses\n    <code>\n     Object.observe()\n    </code>\n    with properties of type\n    <code>\n     Object\n    </code>\n    and\n    <code>\n     Array\n    </code>\n    .\n      To support this on browsers that don\'t support\n    <code>\n     Object.observe()\n    </code>\n    , add a\n    <a href="https://github.com/MaxArt2501/object-observe">\n     polyfill\n    </a>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    The generated directives may be applied only after the custom elements have been registered.\n      This means that in browsers that don\'t support custom elements and rely on the polyfill, the generated directives\n      can be used only after the\n    <code>\n     WebComponentsReady\n    </code>\n    event has been fired. If the initial view of the Angular\n      application contains these directives, you may want to consider manual bootstrap like so:\n   </p>\n   <pre class="prettyprint prettyprinted"><span class="pln">window</span><span class="pun">.</span><span class="pln">addEventListener</span><span class="pun">(</span><span class="str">\'WebComponentsReady \'</span><span class="pun">,</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="kwd">function</span><span class="pun">()</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="pun">{</span><span class="pln">\n  angular</span><span class="pun">.</span><span class="pln">bootstrap</span><span class="pun">(</span><span class="pln">wrap</span><span class="pun">(</span><span class="pln">document</span><span class="pun">),</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="pun">[</span><span class="str">\'ng-polymer-elements-example\'</span><span class="pun">]);</span><span class="pln">\n</span><span class="pun">});</span></pre>\n   <hr/>\n   <h3>\n    Show me "ericbidelman"\n    }\n  ]\n}</pre>\n    </div>\n   </div>\n   <hr/>\n   <h3>\n    How do I use it with other custom elements?\n   </h3>\n   <p>\n    ng-polymer-elements uses a simple structure to map directive attributes to custom element properties.\n      You can extend the mapping by setting the\n    <code>\n     $ngPolymerMappings\n    </code>\n    constant in the\n    <code>\n     ng-polymer-elements\n    </code>\n    module with your mappings.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    The mapping structure is an object where the keys are the directive names, and their values are objects that contain a key\n      for each directive attribute you want to map. The values for the directives represent the custom element property or event,\n      and can be constant or defined in runtime for each instance of the directive.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    For constant mapping, use a string prefixed with "=" for property or "&amp;" for event, and the property/event name.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    For dynamic mapping, use a function named "property" or "event". The function received the element as a single argument\n      during the directive linking and returns a property/event name as string (without "="/"&amp;" prefix).\n   </p>\n   <pre class="prettyprint prettyprinted"><span class="pln">angular</span><span class="pun">.</span><span class="kwd">module</span><span class="pun">(</span><span class="str">\'ng-polymer-elements\'</span><span class="pun">).</span><span class="pln">constant</span><span class="pun">(</span><span class="str">\'$ngPolymerMappings\'</span><span class="pun">,</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="pun">{</span><span class="pln">\n  myElement</span><span class="pun">:</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="pun">{</span><span class="pln">\n    ngModel</span><span class="pun">:</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="kwd">function</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="kwd">property</span><span class="pun">(</span><span class="pln">element</span><span class="pun">)</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="pun">{</span><span class="pln">\n      </span><span class="kwd">return</span><span class="pln"> element</span><span class="pun">.</span><span class="pln">hasAttribute</span><span class="pun">(</span><span class="str">\'multi\'</span><span class="pun">)</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="pun">?</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="str">\'selectedValues\'</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="pun">:</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="str">\'selected\'</span><span class="pun">;</span><span class="pln">\n    </span><span class="pun">},</span><span class="pln">\n    ngChange</span><span class="pun">:</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="str">\'&amp;iron-change\'</span><span class="pln">\n  </span><span class="pun">}</span><span class="pln">\n</span><span class="pun">});</span></pre>\n   <p>\n    In this example we add support for\n    <code>\n     my-element\n    </code>\n    and map the\n    <code>\n     ng-model\n    </code>\n    attribute in runtime to either\n    <code>\n     selectedValue\n    </code>\n    or\n    <code>\n     selected\n    </code>\n    property, depending on the existence of the\n    <code>\n     multi\n    </code>\n    attribute,\n      and we map the\n    <code>\n     ng-change\n    </code>\n    attribute to the\n    <code>\n     iron-change\n    </code>\n    event.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    When mapping events, the original event will be available to AngularJS handlers as the\n    <code>\n     $event\n    </code>\n    parameter.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    See\n    <code>\n     allMappings\n    </code>\n    in\n    <a href="https://github.com/GabiAxel/ng-polymer-elements/blob/master/ng-polymer-elements.js">\n     ng-polymer-elements.js\n    </a>\n    for default mappings.\n   </p>\n  </div>\n  <script
